Conditions for Tahlil: The Requirement of Consummation
Explains the requirement of consummation for tahlil with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for a woman divorced three times to become lawful for her first husband and explain why consummation is required based on Quran and sunnah.

Core Idea
Without genuine consummation by a second husband, a triple-divorced woman remains forever unlawful to her first husband.

This lesson examines the strict conditions Allah has placed on remarriage after a third divorce. The Quranic verse 'until she marries another husband' has been understood by the Hanafi school to require more than a paper marriage—it requires actual consummation. We will unpack the ruling, its proof, and the consequences of violating this divine boundary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
We are looking at the ruling of tahlil—the process by which a triple-divorced woman becomes lawful for her first husband. The act is the marriage and consummation with a second husband.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 2:230 is cited. Note it is qat'i in transmission but zanni in dalala (meaning).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Why does 'marry' include consummation? The Hanafis argue based on the Prophet's practice and Companion understanding.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Saeed ibn al-Musayyib held that marriage alone suffices, but he retracted; Hanafis reject his view.
5
Evaluate the conditions
The text details that insertion must be with the man's own strength and he must experience pleasure; this ensures the marriage is genuine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وينكح مبانته في العدة وبعدها أي المبانة بما دون الثلاث لأن المحلية باقية لأن زوالها معلق بالطلقة الثالثة فينعدم قبلها ومنع الغير في العدة لاشتباه النسب ولا اشتباه في الإطلاق له قوله : (لا) المبانة بالثلاث لو حرة وبالثنتين لو أمة حتى يطأها غيره ولو مراهقاً بنكاح صحيح وتمضي عدته لا بملك يمين أي لا ينكح مبانته بالبينونة الغليظة. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان قبل الدخول أو بعده كما صرح به في الأصل، وأما ما عن المشكلات فيمن طلق امرأته قبل الدخول بها ثلاثاً فله أن يتزوجها بلا تحليل. وأما قوله تعالى ﴿فإن طلقها فلا تحل من بعد حتى تنكح زوجاً غيره ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۳۰] ففي المدخول بها ا هـ. فمعناه أنه طلقها ثلاثاً متفرقة فلا يقع إلا بالأولى لا الثلاث بكلمة واحدة كما ذكره العلامة البخاري شارح الدرر فحينئذ لا حاجة إلى ما في فتح القدير من أنها زلة عظيمة إلى أن قال لا يبعد إكفار مخالفه. وفي القنية أن سعيد بن المسيب رضي الله عنه رجع عن مذهبه في أن الدخول بها ليس بشرط في صيرورتها حلالاً للأول ولو قضى به قاض لا ينفذ قضاؤه، فإن شرط الدخول ثبت بالآثار المشهورة. م فع: يحتال في التطليقات الثلاث ويأخذ الرشى بذلك ويزوجها للأول بدون دخول الثاني هل يصح النكاح وما جزاء من يفعل ذلك قالوا: أن وجهه ويبعد. فع فقيه يفتي بمذهب سعيد بن المسيب ويزوج للأول قال : بقيت مطلقة بثلاث ويعزر الفقيه ا هـ . وأشار بالوطء إلى أن الشرط الإيلاج بشرط كونه عن قوة نفسه وإن كان ملفوفاً بخرقة إذا كان يجد لذة حرارة المحل، فلو أولج الشيخ الكبير الذي لا يقدر على الجماع لا بقوته بل بمساعدة اليد لا يحلها للأول إلا إن انتعش وعمل بخلاف من في فصل فيما تحل به المطلقة
His saying: (And he may marry his irrevocably divorced woman during iddah and after) meaning the woman divorced less than three times, because permissibility remains as its removal is suspended on the third divorce, so it is absent before it. And preventing others during iddah is due to lineage confusion, and no confusion for him after final divorce. His saying: (No) the woman irrevocably divorced by three if free and by two if slave until another man has intercourse with her, even if a boy reaching puberty, in a valid marriage, and her iddah passes, not by ownership of a slave woman. That is, he may not marry his woman with severe irrevocable divorce. He made it absolute, so it includes whether before or after consummation, as stated in al-Asl. As for what is in al-Mushkilat regarding one who divorced his wife three times before consummation, he may marry her without [the need for] tahlil. And His saying {And if he divorces her, she is not lawful to him after until she marries another husband} [2:230] applies to the consummated one. So its meaning is that he divorced her three times separately, so it does not apply except to the first, not three in one word, as mentioned by Allamah Bukhari, sharh al-Durar. Then there is no need for what is in Fath al-Qadir that it is a great slip, until he said that it is not far to declare its violator a disbeliever. In al-Qunyah, that Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, may Allah be pleased with him, retracted his opinion that consummation is not a condition for her becoming lawful for the first, and if a judge rules according to it, his ruling is not executed. For the condition of consummation is established by well-known traditions. A faqih who performs a trick for triple divorces and takes a bribe for it, and marries her to the first without the second's consummation: Is the marriage valid and what is the penalty for the doer? They said: His face is flawed and it is unlikely. A faqih who gives fatwa according to Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and marries her to the first: He said: She remains divorced by three and the faqih is disciplined (ta'zir). And he indicated by 'intercourse' that the condition is insertion, provided it is by his own strength, even if wrapped in a cloth, if he feels the pleasure of the heat of the place. So if an old man who cannot have intercourse inserts not by his strength but by the help of his hand, she does not become lawful for the first unless he becomes erect and performs, unlike the one who is in the chapter on what makes a divorced woman lawful.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the conditions for a woman divorced three times (or two for a slave) to become lawful for her first husband. The author begins with the general rule: a woman divorced less than three times can be remarried by her husband in iddah or after. But if she is divorced three times (free) or two (slave), she cannot be remarried until she marries another man and he consummates the marriage, then she goes through iddah. This applies whether the divorce was before or after consummation. There is a reported opinion from Saeed ibn al-Musayyib that consummation is not required, but he retracted it; Hanafis reject that view. Trickery (tahlil without actual intercourse) is invalid: if a faqih facilitates such a sham marriage, his ruling is void and he is subject to ta'zir. The actual condition for tahlil is that the second husband must insert his penis with his own strength, even if wrapped in a cloth, and he must experience some pleasure. If an elderly man cannot perform without assistance, it does not fulfill the condition unless he becomes erect and performs naturally. This ensures that the marriage is genuine and not a mere ruse.

Key Terms
تحليل (tahlil): The process by which a woman divorced three times becomes lawful for her first husband through marriage and consummation with a second husband.
بينونة غليظة (baynunah ghalizah): Severe irrevocable divorce, i.e., third divorce (or second for a slave) that prevents remarriage without tahlil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is required for a woman divorced three times to become lawful for her first husband?
A) Only marriage to another man.
B) Marriage and consummation with another man.
C) Marriage and two witnesses.
D) A fatwa from a scholar.

Key Takeaway
A triple-divorced woman can only remarry her first husband after a genuine marriage and consummation with a second husband; any trick to avoid this is invalid and sinful.

Multiple Husbands and the Elderly Man in Tahlil
Adds two specific tahlil cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for tahlil, including the requirement of genuine intercourse, and apply them to cases of multiple prior divorces and elderly men.

Core Idea
One valid consummation with a new husband removes prohibition for all previous husbands, provided the intercourse is genuine.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two specific scenarios within the rules of tahlil (making a thrice-divorced woman lawful for her first husband). First, it addresses the rare case of a woman divorced multiple times by different husbands. Second, it emphasizes that the second husband's intercourse must be truly his own act, not assisted. These rulings underscore that the purpose of tahlil is a legitimate marital union, not a mere loophole.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Locate the two distinct cases: (a) a woman divorced thrice by multiple husbands before consummation, then marries another and consummates; (b) an elderly man who inserts with manual assistance. Note the ruling for each.
The first ruling says she becomes lawful for all previous husbands; the second says the elderly man's action does not count unless he achieves natural erection.
2
Understand the underlying condition (shart)
Both cases hinge on the condition of 'ilaj' (insertion) being by the husband's own sexual strength. The passage states the condition is 'insertion provided it is by his own strength' and that he 'feels the pleasure of the heat of the place.' This is the standard Hanafi position.
Even if wrapped in a cloth, the feeling indicates genuine intercourse.
3
Apply the rulings to similar scenarios
Consider other examples: a woman divorced by two different husbands, or a man with partial erectile dysfunction. Determine whether the tahlil is valid based on the condition of genuine, self-powered penetration.

Source Text

وشمل ما إذا طلقها أزواج كل زوج ثلاثاً قبل الدخول فتزوجت بآخر فدخل بها تحل للكل . وأشار بالوطء إلى أن الشرط الإيلاج بشرط كونه عن قوة نفسه وإن كان ملفوفاً بخرقة إذا كان يجد لذة حرارة المحل، فلو أولج الشيخ الكبير الذي لا يقدر على الجماع لا بقوته بل بمساعدة اليد لا يحلها للأول إلا إن انتعش وعمل بخلاف من في فصل فيما تحل به المطلقة
And it includes the case when husbands divorce her, each husband three times before consummation, then she marries another and he penetrates her, she becomes lawful for all. And he indicated by 'intercourse' that the condition is insertion provided it is by his own strength, even if wrapped in a cloth, if he feels the pleasure of the heat of the place. So if an old man who cannot have intercourse inserts not by his strength but by the help of his hand, she does not become lawful for the first unless he becomes erect and performs, unlike the one who is in the chapter on what makes a divorced woman lawful.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This brief passage adds two specific rulings. First, if a woman is divorced by multiple husbands, each having divorced her three times (presumably before consummation, so the divorces were not final), and then she marries another man and he consummates, that single consummation makes her lawful for all previous husbands. This is because the prohibition is removed by the tahlil. Second, the condition for tahlil is that the second husband's insertion must be with his own sexual strength. If an elderly man who is impotent inserts with the help of his hand, it does not fulfill the condition unless he becomes erect and performs naturally. This ensures genuine marital relations.

Key Terms
إيلاج (ilaj): Penetration; the minimal required act for tahlil in the Hanafi school.
قوة نفسه (quwwat nafsih): By his own strength; the condition that the husband's penetration be a result of his own sexual capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a woman is divorced thrice by multiple husbands before consummation and then marries a final husband who consummates by his own strength, what is the ruling?
A) She becomes lawful only for the most recent previous husband.
B) She becomes lawful for all previous husbands.
C) She does not become lawful for any because the divorces were before consummation.
D) She becomes lawful only if the final husband also divorces her three times.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a valid tahlil requires the second husband's penetration by his own sexual strength, and one such consummation suffices for all previous thrice-divorced husbands.

The Core Ruling: Intercourse as the Condition for Tahlil
Commentary on the core ruling and its proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position regarding the condition of intercourse for a thrice-divorced woman and identify the Quranic proof and the rejection of the opposing view.

Core Idea
A thrice-divorced woman becomes halal to her first husband only after actual intercourse (iltiqa' al-khitanayn) with a second husband in a valid marriage.

This lesson examines the foundational ruling from the Hanafi school on tahlil. The commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the Quranic verse 'until she marries another husband' is interpreted to require consummation, supported by prophetic tradition, and that any contrary opinion (like that of Sa'id bin al-Musayyib) is not upheld.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Pinpoint the legal scenario: a thrice-divorced woman (free) or twice-divorced slave woman. The ruling is that she cannot return to her first husband until she marries another man and he consummates the marriage.
The term 'mubāna' refers to irrevocable divorce.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Quranic proof cited: Surah al-Baqarah 2:230. The commentator uses it to establish the necessity of a second marriage.
The verse is قَاطِع (definitive in transmission).
3
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the Hanafi school interprets 'marries' (tankih) to include intercourse. They rely on supplementary evidence (athar) from prophetic practice that the condition is not mere contract but consummation.
The phrase 'حتى تنكح' implies both marriage and intimacy.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Consider the opposing view of Sa'id bin al-Musayyib that marriage alone suffices. The text rejects this, stating it contradicts well-known traditions and that any judgment based on it is unenforceable.
This ikhtilaf has no practical weight in the Hanafi school.
5
Confirm the position
Summarize that the Hanafi school firmly conditions tahlil on actual penetration (iltiqa' al-khitanayn), not just the marriage contract.
This is the mufta bihi position.

A section on what makes the divorced woman permissible. His statement: 'And he marries his irrevocably divorced woman during and after the waiting period' – meaning the one divorced with less than three revocably, because permissibility remains, since its removal is suspended on the third divorce, so it ceases before it. And preventing marriage during the waiting period is due to confusion of lineage, but there is no confusion when the divorce is absolute. His statement: 'Not' the one divorced three times if free, and twice if a slave, until another man, even an adolescent, marries her in a valid marriage and her waiting period passes, not by right hand possession' – meaning he does not marry his irrevocably divorced woman with severe separation. He made it absolute, so it includes whether before or after consummation as clarified in the original. As for what is reported in al-Mushkilat about one who divorces his wife three times before consummation, he may marry her without tahlil. And as for the Almighty's saying: 'If he divorces her, she is not permissible for him after that until she marries another husband' [al-Baqarah 2:230] – that is for the consummated one. So its meaning is that he divorced three times separately, so only the first occurs, not three with one word, as mentioned by al-Allamah al-Bukhari, commentator of al-Durar. Thus there is no need for what is in Fath al-Qadir that it is a great error, to the point that he said it is not far to declare the opponent an unbeliever. In al-Qunyah it is reported that Sa'id bin al-Musayyib, may Allah be pleased with him, retracted his opinion that consummation is not a condition for her becoming permissible to the first husband, and if a judge rules by it, his judgment is not enforced, for the condition of consummation is established by well-known traditions. Then: 'They devise tricks for three divorces and take bribes thereby and marry her to the first husband without entry of the second. Is the marriage valid and what is the punishment for one who does that?' They said: its face is far. So a jurist who gives fatwa according to Sa'id's opinion and marries her to the first husband said: she remains thrice-divorced and the jurist is disciplined. It includes if husbands divorced each husband three times before consummation, then she married another and he consummated, she becomes permissible to all. And he indicated by 'intercourse' that the condition is insertion, provided it is by his own strength, even if wrapped in a cloth if he feels the pleasure of the organ's heat. So if an old man who cannot have intercourse inserts not by his strength but with the help of his hand, it does not make her permissible to the first unless he has an erection and works. In contrast, one whose organ is flaccid and inserts until the circumcised parts meet, then she becomes permissible through him. And excluded is the eunuch who has nothing left to insert into the circumcised area, so she does not become permissible by his grinding until she becomes pregnant. And the castrated man who can copulate like him is included, so he makes her permissible. He meant by 'adolescent' one who can copulate, his organ moves, and he desires intercourse, and Shams al-A'imma estimated it as ten years. He distinguished the young child who cannot copulate, so he does not make her permissible. He made 'intercourse' absolute, so it includes if he had intercourse during menstruation, postpartum bleeding, or ihram, even if unlawful. It includes whether the second husband is Muslim or dhimmi, so a dhimmi woman becomes permissible to her Muslim husband by the intercourse of a dhimmi. And it is the same whether he is free or slave. Thus they said: if she fears her matter appearing in the tahlil, she gives the price of a slave to one she trusts, who buys for her an adolescent, marries her to him with two witnesses, then gifts the slave to her, so the marriage is annulled, then she sends the slave to another country, so her matter does not appear. This is based on the apparent school that compatibility in marriage is not a condition for validity. However, according to the narration of al-Hasan that is given fatwa by, the slave does not make her permissible due to lack of compatibility, but on condition that she has a guardian; if she has no guardian, then it makes her permissible by agreement. And it is better that he be a free adult, for Malik requires orgasm as in al-Bazzaziyyah. He indicated by 'intercourse' that the woman must be one like whom one has intercourse; if she is a young child who is not like whom one has intercourse, she does not become permissible to the first husband by this intercourse. And also that certainty of it being in the right place is necessary; if the woman is mufda (perforated abdomen), she does not become permissible to the first husband after the second's entry unless she becomes pregnant, to know that the intercourse was in her vagina. In al-Qunyah: if the muhallil inserts into the hymen place, she becomes permissible to the first, and death does not stand in place of entry in terms of tahlil. And it is narrated in al-Muhit from the book of Taharah that if a man had intercourse with a virgin, he is not obligated to perform ghusl unless he ejaculated, because the hymen prevents concealment of the glans. He meant by 'valid marriage' the effective one, so the invalid and suspended marriage is excluded. So if a slave married her without his master's permission and then had intercourse before ratification, it does not make her permissible unless he has intercourse after ratification. He indicated that orgasm is not a condition because it is excessive. Included in his statement 'not by right hand possession' are three pictures: first, if a slave woman was divorced by her husband twice and her waiting period passed, then her master has intercourse with her, she does not become permissible to her husband. Second, if the husband buys her after two divorces, she does not become permissible to him by his intercourse until she marries another. Third, if he had a free woman under him, he divorced her three times, then she apostatized and joined the land of war, then he captured her, she does not become permissible to him until she marries another husband. And (He meant by 'adolescent'): al-Ramli said: In Sharh al-Nafi' for the author: if an adolescent had intercourse before puberty, he must divorce her after puberty because divorce from him before puberty is not valid; mentioned in Jami' al-Fatawa. His statement: (In al-Qunyah the muhallil if he inserts etc.) said in al-Nahr: it seems weak, for in the Sharh it is conditioned that the insertion must necessitate ghusl, and this is not so, for in Taharat al-Muhit: if a man had intercourse with a woman etc. His statement: (Included in his statement 'not by right hand possession') three pictures. It is mentioned in al-Nahr that the inclusion of the second and third is far from far. Because the author's statement 'not the divorced one until another man has intercourse with her' means he does not marry the divorced one until another man has intercourse with her, so the negated is the absence...
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the section of talaq concerning what makes a thrice-divorced woman permissible to remarry her first husband. The commentator explains the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The central ruling: a free woman divorced three times (or a slave divorced twice) cannot return to her first husband until she marries another man in a valid marriage, he consummates the marriage with actual intercourse, then she is divorced or widowed and completes her 'idda. The commentator clarifies that this applies regardless of whether the first divorce was before or after consummation. He cites the Quranic verse (2:230) as evidence, noting that the condition of intercourse is established by well-known hadith. The passage then details the conditions of valid intercourse: the second husband must be capable of penetration, and the insertion must be by his own strength, even if he is wrapped in a cloth. An old man who cannot achieve erection without help does not count, unless he becomes erect and performs intercourse. The second husband may be an adolescent who is capable of intercourse, estimated at ten years by Shams al-A'imma. The intercourse must be in the vagina; if the woman is mufda (with a perforated abdomen), she must become pregnant to confirm penetration. The marriage must be valid (sahih nafidh), so a fasid or mawquf marriage does not suffice. There is a note that Imam Malik requires orgasm, but the Hanafi school does not, as penetration (iltiqa' al-khitanayn) is sufficient. The passage also discusses a trick (hila) involving buying a slave, marrying him, then gifting him to the woman to annul the marriage, which is permissible according to the apparent madhhab because compatibility is not a condition, though the fatwa according to al-Hasan's narration requires compatibility for the validity of the marriage if she has a guardian. Finally, three scenarios are given to illustrate that a master's intercourse with his slave woman or a husband's purchase of his divorced wife does not count as tahlil; she must marry a third party.

Key Terms
مبانة (mubāna): A woman who has been divorced irrevocably (with three divorces for a free woman or two for a slave).
تحليل (taḥlīl): The process by which a thrice-divorced woman becomes permissible (halal) to remarry her first husband through a valid marriage and intercourse with a second husband.
إيلاج (īlāj): Insertion of the male organ into the female vagina, which is the condition for tahlīl.
مراهق (murāhiq): An adolescent boy who is close to puberty and capable of sexual intercourse.
كفاءة (kafā'a): Compatibility between spouses in matters like lineage, wealth, and profession, relevant to the validity of the second marriage for tahlīl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a thrice-divorced woman can only remarry her first husband after which of the following conditions is met?
A) She marries a second man and he divorces her immediately without consummation.
B) She marries a second man and he consummates the marriage with actual penetration.
C) She marries a second man but the marriage is fasid (invalid).
D) She marries a second man who is a slave and she has a guardian who disagrees.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school firmly conditions tahlil on actual intercourse, not just marriage.

Conditions of the Second Marriage and the Question of Compatibility
Commentary on conditions of the second marriage and the compatibility dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid second marriage for tahlil and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the requirement of compatibility (kafa'a).

Core Idea
The second marriage must be valid (sahih nafidh) and the husband capable of intercourse; compatibility is not required in the apparent madhhab but is required in the fatwa according to al-Hasan when the woman has a guardian.

This lesson examines the detailed conditions for the second marriage that enables tahlil. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the marriage must be valid and effective, not fasid or mawquf, and that the second husband must be capable of intercourse. It also discusses a trick (hila) that exploits the absence of the compatibility requirement, and notes an alternative position requiring compatibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions of the second marriage
The text states that the marriage must be 'sahih nafidh' (valid and effective). Invalid (fasid) or suspended (mawquf) marriages do not count.
Example of mawquf: a slave marrying without his master's permission before ratification.
2
Examine the husband's capability
The husband must be able to copulate. This excludes a eunuch (majbub) who has nothing left to insert. A castrated man (khasi) who can still copulate is included. An adolescent (murāhiq) of about ten years qualifies if he can copulate.
The condition is based on actual capability, not just age.
3
Analyze the issue of compatibility (kafa'a)
According to the apparent madhhab, compatibility is not a condition for the validity of the second marriage for tahlil. Therefore, a slave can serve as the second husband. However, according to the narration of al-Hasan (which is given fatwa by when the woman has a guardian), compatibility is required, so a slave would not suffice.
If she has no guardian, then even by al-Hasan's narration, a slave suffices by agreement.
4
Consider the practical hila
The text presents a stratagem for a woman who fears her situation will become known: she gives money to a trustee who buys an adolescent slave, marries her to him, then gifts the slave to her, annulling the marriage. She then sends the slave away.
This hila relies on the apparent madhhab that does not require compatibility.
5
Note other conditions and exceptions
The marriage must be with a woman who is capable of intercourse (not a minor who is not yet suitable). If the woman is mufda (perforated), she must become pregnant to confirm penetration. Death does not replace intercourse. The marriage must be valid: if it is fasid (e.g., marriage without witnesses) it does not suffice.
Orgasm is not required; penetration is sufficient.

مخالفه. وفي القنية أن سعيد بن المسيب رضي الله عنه رجع عن مذهبه في أن الدخول بها ليس بشرط في صيرورتها حلالاً للأول ولو قضى به قاض لا ينفذ قضاؤه، فإن شرط الدخول ثبت بالآثار المشهورة. م فع: يحتال في التطليقات الثلاث ويأخذ الرشى بذلك ويزوجها للأول بدون دخول الثاني هل يصح النكاح وما جزاء من يفعل ذلك قالوا: أن وجهه ويبعد. فع فقيه يفتي بمذهب سعيد بن المسيب ويزوج للأول قال : بقيت مطلقة بثلاث ويعزر الفقيه ا هـ . وشمل ما إذا طلقها أزواج كل زوج ثلاثاً قبل الدخول فتزوجت بآخر فدخل بها تحل للكل . وأشار بالوطء إلى أن الشرط الإيلاج بشرط كونه عن قوة نفسه وإن كان ملفوفاً بخرقة إذا كان يجد لذة حرارة المحل، فلو أولج الشيخ الكبير الذي لا يقدر على الجماع لا بقوته بل بمساعدة اليد لا يحلها للأول إلا إن انتعش وعمل بخلاف من في آلته فتور وأولجها فيها حتى التقى الختانان فإنها تحل به . وخرج المجبوب الذي لم A section on what makes the divorced woman permissible. His statement: 'And he marries his irrevocably divorced woman during and after the waiting period' – meaning the one divorced with less than three revocably, because permissibility remains, since its removal is suspended on the third divorce, so it ceases before it. And preventing marriage during the waiting period is due to confusion of lineage, but there is no confusion when the divorce is absolute. His statement: 'Not' the one divorced three times if free, and twice if a slave, until another man, even an adolescent, marries her in a valid marriage and her waiting period passes, not by right hand possession' – meaning he does not marry his irrevocably divorced woman with severe separation. He made it absolute, so it includes whether before or after consummation as clarified in the original. As for what is reported in al-Mushkilat about one who divorces his wife three times before consummation, he may marry her without tahlil. And as for the Almighty's saying: 'If he divorces her, she is not permissible for him after that until she marries another husband' [al-Baqarah 2:230] – that is for the consummated one. So its meaning is that he divorced three times separately, so only the first occurs, not three with one word, as mentioned by al-Allamah al-Bukhari, commentator of al-Durar. Thus there is no need for what is in Fath al-Qadir that it is a great error, to the point that he said it is not far to declare the opponent an unbeliever. In al-Qunyah it is reported that Sa'id bin al-Musayyib, may Allah be pleased with him, retracted his opinion that consummation is not a condition for her becoming permissible to the first husband, and if a judge rules by it, his judgment is not enforced, for the condition of consummation is established by well-known traditions. Then: 'They devise tricks for three divorces and take bribes thereby and marry her to the first husband without entry of the second. Is the marriage valid and what is the punishment for one who does that?' They said: its face is far. So a jurist who gives fatwa according to Sa'id's opinion and marries her to the first husband said: she remains thrice-divorced and the jurist is disciplined. It includes if husbands divorced each husband three times before consummation, then she married another and he consummated, she becomes permissible to all. And he indicated by 'intercourse' that the condition is insertion, provided it is by his own strength, even if wrapped in a cloth if he feels the pleasure of the organ's heat. So if an old man who cannot have intercourse inserts not by his strength but with the help of his hand, it does not make her permissible to the first unless he has an erection and works. In contrast, one whose organ is flaccid and inserts until the circumcised parts meet, then she becomes permissible through him. And excluded is the eunuch who has nothing left to insert into the circumcised area, so she does not become permissible by his grinding until she becomes pregnant. And the castrated man who can copulate like him is included, so he makes her permissible. He meant by 'adolescent' one who can copulate, his organ moves, and he desires intercourse, and Shams al-A'imma estimated it as ten years. He distinguished the young child who cannot copulate, so he does not make her permissible. He made 'intercourse' absolute, so it includes if he had intercourse during menstruation, postpartum bleeding, or ihram, even if unlawful. It includes whether the second husband is Muslim or dhimmi, so a dhimmi woman becomes permissible to her Muslim husband by the intercourse of a dhimmi. And it is the same whether he is free or slave. Thus they said: if she fears her matter appearing in the tahlil, she gives the price of a slave to one she trusts, who buys for her an adolescent, marries her to him with two witnesses, then gifts the slave to her, so the marriage is annulled, then she sends the slave to another country, so her matter does not appear. This is based on the apparent school that compatibility in marriage is not a condition for validity. However, according to the narration of al-Hasan that is given fatwa by, the slave does not make her permissible due to lack of compatibility, but on condition that she has a guardian; if she has no guardian, then it makes her permissible by agreement. And it is better that he be a free adult, for Malik requires orgasm as in al-Bazzaziyyah. He indicated by 'intercourse' that the woman must be one like whom one has intercourse; if she is a young child who is not like whom one has intercourse, she does not become permissible to the first husband by this intercourse. And also that certainty of it being in the right place is necessary; if the woman is mufda (perforated abdomen), she does not become permissible to the first husband after the second's entry unless she becomes pregnant, to know that the intercourse was in her vagina. In al-Qunyah: if the muhallil inserts into the hymen place, she becomes permissible to the first, and death does not stand in place of entry in terms of tahlil. And it is narrated in al-Muhit from the book of Taharah that if a man had intercourse with a virgin, he is not obligated to perform ghusl unless he ejaculated, because the hymen prevents concealment of the glans. He meant by 'valid marriage' the effective one, so the invalid and suspended marriage is excluded. So if a slave married her without his master's permission and then had intercourse before ratification, it does not make her permissible unless he has intercourse after ratification. He indicated that orgasm is not a condition because it is excessive. Included in his statement 'not by right hand possession' are three pictures: first, if a slave woman was divorced by her husband twice and her waiting period passed, then her master has intercourse with her, she does not become permissible to her husband. Second, if the husband buys her after two divorces, she does not become permissible to him by his intercourse until she marries another. Third, if he had a free woman under him, he divorced her three times, then she apostatized and joined the land of war, then he captured her, she does not become permissible to him until she marries another husband. And (He meant by 'adolescent'): al-Ramli said: In Sharh al-Nafi' for the author: if an adolescent had intercourse before puberty, he must divorce her after puberty because divorce from him before puberty is not valid; mentioned in Jami' al-Fatawa. His statement: (In al-Qunyah the muhallil if he inserts etc.) said in al-Nahr: it seems weak, for in the Sharh it is conditioned that the insertion must necessitate ghusl, and this is not so, for in Taharat al-Muhit: if a man had intercourse with a woman etc. His statement: (Included in his statement 'not by right hand possession') three pictures. It is mentioned in al-Nahr that the inclusion of the second and third is far from far. Because the author's statement 'not the divorced one until another man has intercourse with her' means he does not marry the divorced one until another man has intercourse with her, so the negated is the absence...
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the section of talaq concerning what makes a thrice-divorced woman permissible to remarry her first husband. The commentator explains the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The central ruling: a free woman divorced three times (or a slave divorced twice) cannot return to her first husband until she marries another man in a valid marriage, he consummates the marriage with actual intercourse, then she is divorced or widowed and completes her 'idda. The commentator clarifies that this applies regardless of whether the first divorce was before or after consummation. He cites the Quranic verse (2:230) as evidence, noting that the condition of intercourse is established by well-known hadith. The passage then details the conditions of valid intercourse: the second husband must be capable of penetration, and the insertion must be by his own strength, even if he is wrapped in a cloth. An old man who cannot achieve erection without help does not count, unless he becomes erect and performs intercourse. The second husband may be an adolescent who is capable of intercourse, estimated at ten years by Shams al-A'imma. The intercourse must be in the vagina; if the woman is mufda (with a perforated abdomen), she must become pregnant to confirm penetration. The marriage must be valid (sahih nafidh), so a fasid or mawquf marriage does not suffice. There is a note that Imam Malik requires orgasm, but the Hanafi school does not, as penetration (iltiqa' al-khitanayn) is sufficient. The passage also discusses a trick (hila) involving buying a slave, marrying him, then gifting him to the woman to annul the marriage, which is permissible according to the apparent madhhab because compatibility is not a condition, though the fatwa according to al-Hasan's narration requires compatibility for the validity of the marriage if she has a guardian. Finally, three scenarios are given to illustrate that a master's intercourse with his slave woman or a husband's purchase of his divorced wife does not count as tahlil; she must marry a third party.

Key Terms
مبانة (mubāna): A woman who has been divorced irrevocably (with three divorces for a free woman or two for a slave).
تحليل (taḥlīl): The process by which a thrice-divorced woman becomes permissible (halal) to remarry her first husband through a valid marriage and intercourse with a second husband.
إيلاج (īlāj): Insertion of the male organ into the female vagina, which is the condition for tahlīl.
مراهق (murāhiq): An adolescent boy who is close to puberty and capable of sexual intercourse.
كفاءة (kafā'a): Compatibility between spouses in matters like lineage, wealth, and profession, relevant to the validity of the second marriage for tahlīl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a thrice-divorced woman can only remarry her first husband after which of the following conditions is met?
A) She marries a second man and he divorces her immediately without consummation.
B) She marries a second man and he consummates the marriage with actual penetration.
C) She marries a second man but the marriage is fasid (invalid).
D) She marries a second man who is a slave and she has a guardian who disagrees.

Key Takeaway
The second marriage for tahlil must be valid and consummated; the compatibility of the husband is not a condition in the apparent madhhab, but fatwa may vary when a guardian is present.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Conditions of the Second Husband for Tahlil
Defining conditions and a legal trick for tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the physical conditions required for a muhallil and explain the Hanafi dispute regarding the use of a slave as a muhallil.

Core Idea
A muhallil must achieve full penetration; a slave suffices only if the woman has no guardian.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the essential physical requirements for the second husband (muhallil) to make a triply divorced woman permissible to her first husband. It also addresses an important intra-Hanafi disagreement about whether a slave can serve as a muhallil, reminding us that compatibility (kafa'a) is not a universal condition. Understanding these details is critical for correctly applying the rules of tahlil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the second husband's intercourse with the triply divorced woman. The ruling is that it makes her halal for the first husband, provided specific conditions are met.
The ruling is sahih (valid) and mubah (permissible) in effect, though the intention may affect its desirability.
2
List the physical conditions for the muhallil
Examine the text to extract the requirements: the second husband must achieve full penetration with his organ erect until the two circumcised parts meet. Excluded is the majbub (amputated) who cannot insert. Included is the eunuch who can have intercourse. The murahiq (adolescent) must be at least ten years old and capable of intercourse.
The condition of full penetration is strict; rubbing or partial insertion does not suffice unless pregnancy occurs (for majbub).
3
Analyze the slave issue and the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
According to the apparent madhhab, a slave suffices because kafa'a is not a condition for marriage validity. However, the narration of al-Hasan (mufta bihi) holds that a slave does not make her permissible if she has a guardian, due to lack of compatibility. If she has no guardian, all agree a slave suffices.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that the validity of tahlil with a slave depends on the presence or absence of a guardian.
4
Note the additional condition from Imam Malik
The text mentions that Malik requires ejaculation, which is not required in the Hanafi school. This highlights a cross-madhhab difference.
The Hanafi school only requires penetration; ejaculation is not a condition.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi position
The text states that the narration of al-Hasan is mufta bihi (the relied-upon position). Therefore, in fatwa, a slave is not considered a valid muhallil if the woman has a guardian.
This ruling affects the legal hila (stratagem) described in the passage, which relies on the apparent madhhab.

His organ became erect and he inserted it into her until the two circumcised parts meet, then she becomes permissible to the first husband. Excluded is the one whose penis is cut off (majbub) who has nothing left to insert into the place of circumcision, so she does not become permissible by his rubbing until she becomes pregnant. Included is the eunuch (khasi) who is like one who can have intercourse, so he makes her permissible. By 'murahiq' (adolescent) he means one who can have intercourse, his organ moves, and he desires intercourse; Shams al-Islam estimated him at ten years. He guarded against the young child who cannot have intercourse like him, so he does not make her permissible. He used the absolute term 'intercourse' so it includes when he had intercourse with her during menstruation, post-partum bleeding, or ihram, even if it is forbidden. It includes whether the second husband is Muslim or dhimmi, so a dhimmi woman becomes permissible by the intercourse of a dhimmi to her Muslim husband. It is the same whether he is free or a slave. Therefore they said: If she fears that her matter will become known in the tahlil, she gives to someone she trusts the price of a slave, who buys her a murahiq [adolescent] and marries him to her with two witnesses, then he gifts the slave to her so the marriage is annulled, then she sends the slave to another country so her matter does not become apparent. This is based on the apparent madhhab that compatibility (kafa'a) in marriage is not a condition for validity. But according to the narration of al-Hasan which is given fatwa, a slave does not make her permissible due to lack of compatibility, but on condition that she has a guardian. If she has no guardian, then he makes her permissible by agreement. The better view is that he be free and adult, for Malik requires ejaculation as in al-Bazzaziyya. Along with: (He intended by murahiq, al-Ramli said: In Sharh al-Nafi' by the author: If the adolescent had intercourse with her before puberty, then he must divorce her after puberty because divorce from him before puberty is not valid; mentioned in Jami' al-Fatawa.)
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the physical conditions required for the second husband (al-muhallil) to make a triply divorced woman permissible to her first husband. The text opens by stating that if the second husband achieves full penetration with his organ erect until the two circumcised parts meet, she becomes halal. An exception is made for a majbub (penis amputated) who cannot insert anything; his rubbing does not suffice unless she becomes pregnant. A eunuch who retains the ability to have intercourse is included. The term 'murahiq' is defined as an adolescent who can have intercourse, has erections, and desires sex; Shams al-Islam set the age at ten years. A child younger than that who cannot have intercourse does not make her permissible. The ruling applies even if intercourse occurs during forbidden times (menstruation, post-partum, ihram) because the key is penetration, not permissibility. The second husband can be Muslim or dhimmi, free or slave, according to the apparent madhhab which does not require kafa'a. However, a narration from al-Hasan (muffa biha) holds that a slave cannot be used unless the woman has no guardian, in which case all agree he suffices. The text also presents a legal trick (hila) for a woman who fears exposure: she gives money to a trusted person to buy a slave adolescent, marry him to her, then the slave is gifted to her, annulling the marriage, and then she sends the slave away to hide the matter. Imam Malik's additional condition of ejaculation is noted.

Key Terms
مجبوب (majbub): A man whose penis has been amputated, leaving no part to insert.
مراهق (murahiq): An adolescent boy who is physically capable of intercourse, typically age ten or older.
ختان (khatan): Circumcised part; the phrase 'meeting of the two circumcised parts' is a metaphor for full penetration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what condition must be met for a slave to be a valid muhallil?
A) The slave must be freed before consummation.
B) The woman must have no guardian.
C) The slave must be at least fifteen years old.
D) The slave must ejaculate during intercourse.

Key Takeaway
The muhallil must achieve full penetration; a slave is valid only if the woman has no guardian, per the mufta bihi position.

Conditions of the Woman and Validity of Second Marriage for Tahlil
Expands conditions for tahlil concerning the woman and marriage validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid tahlil, distinguish between cases requiring pregnancy, and explain why ejaculation is not a condition in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tahlil requires vaginal penetration with certainty; for a mufda woman, only pregnancy proves it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on the conditions for tahlil, focusing on the woman's side. It clarifies that the second marriage must be valid and effective, and that penetration must be certain. For a woman with an abnormal vaginal opening (mufda), pregnancy is necessary to confirm vaginal intercourse, while ejaculation is not required. These rulings have practical implications for determining when a woman becomes permissible to her first husband after three divorces.

Guided Path
1
Identify the woman's condition
Determine if the woman is capable of being penetrated. If she is a minor who cannot be penetrated, tahlil does not occur.
The text says: 'la budda an yutaa mithluha' – she must be one who can be penetrated like her.
2
Check certainty of vaginal penetration
Examine if there is certainty that intercourse occurred in the vagina. For a mufda woman, pregnancy is the proof.
Mufda: a woman with a perforated vagina; without pregnancy, we cannot be sure the intercourse was in the proper place.
3
Verify the marriage's validity and effectiveness
The second marriage must be sahih and nafidh (valid and immediately effective). Fasid (irregular) or mawquf (suspended) marriages do not suffice.
Example: a slave marrying without master's permission – if he has intercourse before ratification, it does not count.
4
Recognize that ejaculation is not required
The Hanafi school holds that penetration alone is satiating (mushbi') and suffices; Malik requires ejaculation.
The text states: 'al-inzal laysa bi-shart' – ejaculation is not a condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار بالوطء إلى أن المرأة لا بد أن يوطاً مثلها، أما إذا كانت صغيرة لا يوطأ مثلها لا تحل للأول بهذا الوطء، وإلى أنه لا بد من التيقن بكونه في المحل حق لو كانت المرأة مفضاة لا تحل للأول بعد دخول الثاني إلا إذا حبلت ليعلم أن الوطء كان في قبلها. وفي القنية : المحلل إذا أولج في مكان البكارة تحل للأول والموت لا يقوم مقام الدخول في حق التحليل ا هـ . أنه نقل في المحيط من كتاب الطهارة أنه لو أتى امرأة وهي عذراء لا غسل عليه ما لم ينزل لأن العذرة مانعة من مواراة الخشفة ا.هـ. وأراد بالنكاح الصحيح النافذ فخرج النكاح الفاسد والموقوف كما لو تزوجها عبد بغير إذن سيده ثم وطئها قبل الإجازة لا يحلها إلا إذا وطئها بعد الإجازة. وأشار إلى أن الإنزال ليس بشرط لأنه مشبع.
And by 'intercourse' he indicated that the woman must be one who can be penetrated like her. If she is a minor who cannot be penetrated like her, she does not become permissible to the first by this intercourse. And that it is necessary to be certain that it was in the right place; if the woman is mufda (perforated), she does not become permissible to the first after the second's entry unless she becomes pregnant so that it is known the intercourse was in her vagina. In al-Qunyah: The muhallil if he inserted in the place of virginity, she becomes permissible to the first, and death does not take the place of entry in the matter of tahlil. It is narrated in al-Muhit from the book of Taharah that if a man had intercourse with a virgin, there is no ghusl on him unless he ejaculates because the hymen prevents the concealment of the glans. He intended by the valid and effective marriage, so the invalid (fasid) and suspended (mawquf) marriage are excluded, as when a slave marries her without his master's permission then has intercourse with her before ratification, it does not make her permissible unless he has intercourse after ratification. And he indicated that ejaculation is not a condition because it is satiating.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of tahlil, focusing on the woman's side. It states that the woman must be such that she can be penetrated; a minor who cannot be penetrated does not become permissible by the second husband's intercourse. Furthermore, certainty is required that penetration occurred in the proper place. If the woman is mufda (having a perforated vagina or abnormal opening), she does not become halal unless she becomes pregnant, as pregnancy proves that intercourse was in the vagina. A ruling from al-Qunyah says that if the muhallil inserts in the place of the hymen (i.e., at the opening of the vagina), she becomes permissible; death of the second husband does not substitute for entry. A note from al-Muhit explains that with a virgin, no ghusl is obligatory unless ejaculation occurs, because the hymen prevents concealment of the glans. The passage then clarifies that the marriage must be valid (sahih) and effective (nafidh); an invalid marriage (fasid) or a suspended one (mawquf) does not count. Example: a slave who marries without his master's permission and has intercourse before ratification does not make her halal; she becomes halal only if he has intercourse after the master ratifies the marriage. Finally, ejaculation (inzal) is not a condition for tahlil; penetration alone suffices.

Key Terms
مفضاة (mufda): A woman who has a perforated vagina or abnormal opening such that certainty of vaginal penetration is difficult.
نكاح صحيح نافذ (nikah sahih nafidh): A marriage contract that is both legally valid (sahih) and immediately effective (nafidh), not suspended or invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, what is required for a valid tahlil when the woman is mufda?
A) Ejaculation by the second husband
B) Pregnancy after the second husband's intercourse
C) The second husband must be an adult
D) The marriage must be witnessed by two female witnesses

Key Takeaway
For tahlil, vaginal penetration with certainty is essential; ejaculation is not a condition, but for a mufda woman, pregnancy serves as proof of vaginal intercourse.

Three Cases Where Ownership Does Not Make a Divorced Wife Halal
Explains three scenarios where a husband cannot make his wife halal through ownership

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios where a husband cannot make his divorced wife halal through ownership and explain why ownership alone is insufficient.

Core Idea
Ownership of a divorced wife does not permit intercourse; she must marry another man with consummation.

This lesson examines three specific cases where a divorced wife cannot become halal for her former husband simply because he owns her as a slave. The Hanafi school insists that after a final divorce, mere ownership does not dissolve the prohibition; the wife must undergo a full marriage contract with another who consummates it. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies these cases and addresses a textual nuance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle
After a final divorce (two for a slave woman, three for a free woman), the wife is haram until she marries another man and he consummates the marriage.
This is derived from Qur'an 2:230.
2
Identify the first case
A slave woman divorced twice, then after her 'iddah, her master (who was the husband) has intercourse with her as his slave. Why does this not make her halal? Because she was divorced and needs a new marriage, not mere ownership.
3
Identify the second case
The husband buys her after the two divorces. Does ownership through purchase suffice? No, she must marry another.
4
Identify the third case
A free woman divorced three times, then she apostatizes and is enslaved by the husband. Even though he owns her, she does not become permissible.
5
Note the textual critique
Al-Nahr criticizes that the matn's phrase 'la yamlik yameen' negates marriage, not possession, so including cases 2 and 3 is far-fetched. The correct understanding is that the prohibition covers both marriage and possession, as the verse does.
This is a linguistic refinement, not a difference in ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ودخل في قوله «لا يملك يمين» ثلاث صور : الأولى أن الأمة لو طلقها زوجها ثنتين وانقضت عدتها فوطئها المولى لا تحل لزوجها. الثانية لو اشتراها الزوج بعد الثنتين لا تحل له بوطئه حتى تتزوج بغيره. الثالثة لو كانت تحته حرة فطلقها ثلاثاً ثم ارتدت ولحقت بدار الحرب ثم استرقها لم تحل له حتى تتزوج بزوج آخر . قوله: (ودخل في قوله لا يملك يمين ثلاث صور ذكر في النهر أن دخول الثانية والثالثة فيه أبعد من البعيد ا هـ . لأن قول المصنف لا المبانة حتى يطأها غيره معناه لا ينكح المبانة حتى يطأها غيره فالمغيا عدم النكاح، والذي في المسالتين عدم الوطء بملك اليمين. نعم لو قال المصنف لا ينكح المبانة ولا يطأها يملك اليمين حتى يطأها غيره الخ. لصح ذلك فساوى قوله تعالى فلا تحل له حتى تنكح زوجا غيره ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٣٠] حيث جعل غاية لعدم الحل الشامل لما إذا كان بنكاح أو ملك يمين قوله : (لا تحل له بوطئه حتى تتزوج بغيره لعل الصواب لا تحل له بملكه. قال في البدائع : وكذا إن اشتراها الزوج قبل أن تنكح زوجاً غيره لم تحل بملك اليمين ا هـ . وعبارة الفتح : لو طلقها ثنتين وهي أ أمة ثم ملكها أو ثلاثاً لحرة فارتدت ولحقت ثم ظهر على الدار فملكها لا يحل له وطؤها بملك اليمين حتى يزوجها فيدخل بها الزوج ثم يطلقها
And enters into his statement 'he does not possess a right (yamin)' three scenarios: First, if a slave woman is divorced by her husband twice and her 'iddah expires, then her master has intercourse with her, she does not become permissible to her [first] husband. Second, if the husband buys her after the two divorces, she does not become permissible to him by his intercourse until she marries another. Third, if a free woman under him, he divorces her three times, then she apostatizes and joins the abode of war, then he enslaves her, she does not become permissible to him until she marries another husband. His statement: (And enters into his statement 'he does not possess a right (yamin)' three scenarios. It is mentioned in al-Nahr that the inclusion of the second and third is far-fetched. Because the author's statement 'the separated woman until another has intercourse with her' means he does not marry the separated woman until another has intercourse with her, so the negated is the marriage, and in the two cases the issue is the absence of intercourse by right of possession. Yes, if the author said 'he does not marry the separated woman nor does he have intercourse with her by right of possession until another has intercourse with her' then it would be correct, and it would equal the verse 'she is not lawful for him until she marries another husband' (2:230) which makes the limit for the lack of permissibility general, whether it is by marriage or by possession. His statement: 'she does not become permissible to him by his intercourse until she marries another' - perhaps the correct wording is 'she does not become permissible to him by his ownership.' Said in al-Bada'i: Likewise if the husband buys her before she marries another husband, she does not become permissible by possession. The wording of al-Fath: If he divorces her twice while she is a slave and then owns her, or three times to a free woman who apostatizes and then he owns her, it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her by possession until he marries her to someone who penetrates her and then divorces her.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage discusses the phrase 'la yamlik yameen' (he does not possess a right) from the matn, explaining three scenarios where a husband cannot make his divorced wife halal through ownership (milk al-yamin) but must instead marry her off to another man. The first case: a slave woman divorced twice by her husband, then after her 'iddah, her master (who was the husband) has intercourse with her as his slave; this does not make her halal for remarriage because she was divorced and needs a separate marriage. The second case: the husband buys her (the slave) after two divorces; his intercourse with her as his property does not make her permissible; she must marry another. The third case: a free woman divorced three times, then she apostatizes and goes to dar al-harb, and the husband later enslaves her; again, ownership does not replace the need for another husband. The passage then critiques the inclusion of the second and third cases under 'la yamlik yameen' because the matn's phrase negates marriage (nikah) not possession. The correct interpretation, according to al-Nahr, is that the verse and the matn refer to the prohibition of both marriage and possession until she marries another. The correct wording in the commentary should be 'she does not become permissible to him by his ownership (milk) until she marries another,' not 'by his intercourse.' References from al-Bada'i' and al-Fath confirm that mere ownership does not make her halal; she must be married to another who consummates.

Key Terms
ملك يمين (milk yamin): Right of possession (ownership) over a slave, which includes the right to sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband divorces his free wife three times, and she then apostatizes and is captured as a slave, can he have intercourse with her by right of ownership?
A) Yes, because he owns her
B) No, she must marry another first
C) Yes, if she converts back
D) No, because apostasy invalidates the marriage

Key Takeaway
After a final divorce, no form of ownership by the husband can make the wife halal; she must marry another man who consummates.

Diyanah vs Qada' in Tahlil When Husband Denies Divorce
Dispute over diyanah permissibility of tahlil when husband denies divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between diyanah and qada' in the case of a wife whose husband denies triple divorce, and state the mufta bihi position that she may remarry for tahlil diyanan.

Core Idea
A woman may remarry diyanan if she knows the divorce, even if a court cannot enforce it.

When a husband denies divorcing his wife three times, a conflict arises between the apparent legal status and the woman's inner certainty. This lesson examines a well-known Hanafi dispute: can she secretly remarry another for tahlil? The text presents the view of Shams al-A'imma al-Auzjandi and others who allow her to do so purely diyanan—between herself and Allah—while other scholars prohibit it. Understanding this distinction is crucial for appreciating how Hanafi fiqh balances evidentiary rules with individual conscience.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
Identify the key facts: a woman has been divorced three times, but her husband denies it and the judge rules in his favor based on apparent evidence.
This is the classical setting for the diyanah vs. qada' conflict.
2
Define the two categories
Distinguish between 'diyanah' (religious duty based on inner knowledge) and 'qada'' (court ruling based on external evidence). The woman knows the truth, but the court cannot act on it.
Diyanah concerns what is binding before Allah; qada' is enforceable by a judge.
3
Identify the Hanafi position on remarriage
State the position of al-Auzjandi and others: she may remarry another (for tahlil) diyanan, though she cannot do so qada'an. Provide the evidence from the text.
The text quotes al-Auzjandi: 'They said this is in the judicial context, but she has the right to do it diyanan.'
4
Identify the opposing view
Some Hanafi scholars hold that even diyanan it is not permissible because she is still legally married until a court separates them. Their evidence is that the marriage is deemed continuing.
The text refers to 'the others' without naming them specifically.
5
Determine the tarjih and its implications
The author (Ibn Nujaym) sides with al-Auzjandi, making the permissibility diyanan the mufta bihi. The practical consequence: the woman can secretly perform tahlil and later return to her first husband without sin, as long as she acts on her certain knowledge.
The tarjih is based on the principle that certainty overrides doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي مناقب البزازي : إذا كان العقد بلا ولي بل بعبارة المرأة أو كان بلفظ الهبة أو كان بحضرة، فاسقين ثم طلقها ثلاثاً ثم أراد أن تحل له بلا زوج فإنه يرفع الأمر إلى شافعي فيقضي ببطلان النكاح وبزوجها له بعقد جديد ولا يرد أن القضاء بفساد النكاح يستلزم حرمة الوطء المتقدم وأن الأولاد متولدة من وطء حرام لأنا نقول : القضاء يعمل في القائم والآتي لا في الماضي ا هـ . وفي فتاويه : وإن حافت أن لا يطلقها المحلل تقول له حتى يقول إن تزوجتك وجامعتك فأنت طالق ا هـ . وأطلق فشمل ما إذا كان الزوج الأول معترفاً بالطلاق الثلاث أو منكراً بعد أن كان الواقع الطلاق الثلاث ولهذا قالوا: لو طلقها ثلاثاً وأنكر لها أن تتزوج بآخر وتحلل نفسها سراً منه إذا غاب في سفر فإذا رجع التمست منه تجديد النكاح لشك خالج قلبها لا لإنكار الزوج النكاح. وقد ذكر في القنية خلافاً فرقم للأصل بأنها إن قدرت على الهروب منه لم يسعها أن تعتد وتتزوج بآخر لأنها في حكم زوجية الأول قبل القضاء بالفرقة، ثم رمز شمس الأئمة الاوزجندي وقال : قالوا هذا في القضاء ولها ذلك ديانة، وكذلك إن سمعته طلقها ثلاثاً ثم جحد وحلف أنه لم يفعل وردها القاضي عليه لم يسعها المقام معه ولم يسعها أن تتزوج بغيره أيضاً. قال - يعني البديع: والحاصل أنه على جواب شمس الإسلام الاوزجندي ونجم الدين النسفي والسيد أبي شجاع وأبي حامد والسرخسي يحل لها أن تتزوج بزوج آخر فيما بينها وبين الله تعالى وعلى جواب الباقين لا يحل انتهى . وفي الفتاوى السراجية : إذا أخبرها ثقة أن الزوج طلقها وهو غائب وسعها أن تعتد وتتزوج ولم يقيده بالديانة والله أعلم . قال المصنف رحمه الله : وقد نقل في القنية قبل ذلك عن شرح السرخسي ما صورته : طلق امرأته ثلاثاً وغاب عنها فلها أن تتزوج بزوج آخر بعد العدة ديانة. ونقل آخر أنه لا يجوز في المذهب الصحيح ا هـ . قلت : إنما رقم لشمس الأئمة الأوزجندي وهو الموافق لما تقدم عنه والقائل بأنه المذهب الصحيح العلاء الترجماني ثم رقم بعده لعمر النسفي وقال : حلف بثلاثة فظن أنه لم يحنث وعلمت الحنث وظنت أنها لو أخبرته ينكر اليمين فإذا غاب عنها بسبب من الأسباب فلها التحلل ديانة لا قضاء.
And in Manaqib al-Bazzazi: If the marriage contract was without a guardian but by the woman's own words, or was with the wording of gift (hiba), or was in the presence of two immoral witnesses, then he divorced her three times, then he wanted to make her permissible to himself without a (second) husband, then he should refer the matter to a Shafi'i judge who will rule the marriage void and marry her to him with a new contract. It is not objected that the ruling of invalidity of the marriage necessitates the prohibition of the previous intercourse and that the children are from forbidden intercourse, because we say: The judgment acts on the present and future, not on the past. And in his Fatawa: If she fears that the muhallil will not divorce her, she says to him: 'Say: If I marry you and have intercourse with you, you are divorced.' And he used the term absolutely, so it includes whether the first husband admits the triple divorce or denies it after the fact of triple divorce. Therefore they said: If he divorced her three times and he denies it, she may marry another and secretly make herself permissible to him (the first) when he is away on a journey, and when he returns she seeks from him a renewal of the marriage due to a doubt that entered her heart, not due to the husband's denial of the marriage. And it has been mentioned in al-Qunyah a difference, and he coded for the principle that if she is able to escape from him, it is not permissible for her to observe 'iddah and marry another because she is in the status of being under the first marriage before the court's decision of separation. Then Shams al-A'imma al-Auzjandi coded and said: They said this is in the judicial (qada') context, but she has the right to do it diyanan. Likewise if she heard him divorce her three times, then he denied and swore that he did not do it, and the judge returned her to him, it is not permissible for her to stay with him and also not permissible for her to marry another. He (al-Badi') said: The summary is that according to the response of Shams al-Islam al-Auzjandi, Najm al-Din al-Nasafi, Sayyid Abi Shuja', Abu Hamid, and al-Sarakhsi, it is permissible for her to marry another husband between herself and Allah, and according to the response of the others it is not permissible. In al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyya: If a trustworthy person informs her that the husband divorced her while he is absent, it is permissible for her to observe 'iddah and marry, and he did not restrict it to diyanah. The author said: And it has been transmitted in al-Qunyah before that from Sharh al-Sarakhsi in the following form: He divorced his wife three times and was absent from her, and she may marry another husband after the 'iddah diyanan. Another narration that it is not permissible in the correct madhhab. I say: He only coded for Shams al-A'imma al-Auzjandi, which is in agreement with what preceded from him, and the one who says it is the correct madhhab is 'Ala' al-Turjumani. Then after him he coded for 'Umar al-Nasafi who said: He swore by three (divorces) thinking he did not break the oath, but she knew he broke it and thought if she told him he would deny the oath; so when he is absent due to some cause, she may make herself permissible diyanan not qada'an.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage discusses the situation where a woman has been divorced three times but her husband denies it. The question is whether she can marry another (for tahlil) secretly. The text presents a trick (hila) from Manaqib al-Bazzazi: if the original marriage was defective (e.g., without a guardian, or with a gift wording, or with immoral witnesses), then the husband can refer the matter to a Shafi'i judge who will rule the marriage invalid and then marry her to him anew. This works because judicial rulings only affect the present and future, not the past. Another hila: if she fears the muhallil won't divorce her, she can have him say, 'If I marry you and have intercourse with you, you are divorced,' so that the divorce is conditional. The general ruling is that if the husband admits the triple divorce, she can remarry openly. If he denies it, she may secretly marry another only diyanan (between herself and Allah), but not qada'an (in court). There is a difference of opinion: some scholars like Shams al-A'imma al-Auzjandi allow her to remarry diyanan; others forbid it even diyanan. The text quotes al-Qunyah and other sources. Al-Sarakhsi's Sharh allows her to remarry diyanan after 'iddah. The author (Ibn Nujaym) sides with al-Auzjandi as the correct madhhab. A scenario: if the husband swore a false oath denying the divorce, and she knows the truth, but he is absent, she may perform tahlil diyanan but not qada'an.

Key Terms
ديانة (diyanatan): In terms of religious obligation before Allah, as opposed to legal enforcement by a court.
قضاء (qada'an): In terms of legal enforcement by a judge based on apparent evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a husband denies divorcing his wife three times, what is the relied-upon Hanafi position regarding her remarrying another for tahlil?
A) She cannot remarry at all
B) She may remarry only qada'an
C) She may remarry diyanan
D) She must wait for the husband's return

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a woman who knows she has been divorced three times may remarry for tahlil diyanan, even if the husband denies it in court.

Qada' vs Diyaanah: A Thrice-Divorced Woman's Options When Husband Denies
Fatwas on secret remarriage and self-defense for the thrice-divorced woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qada' and diyaanah rulings for a thrice-divorced woman, state the Hanafi position on secret remarriage, and evaluate the disagreement on self-defense.

Core Idea
When the husband denies triple divorce, the woman may remarry secretly (diyaanatan) but not in court; killing him is disputed and the fatwa forbids it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a series of fatwas addressing the plight of a woman whose husband has divorced her three times but denies it. The central tension is between what is enforceable in court (qada') and what is permissible before Allah (diyaanah). We will explore the opinions of major Hanafi scholars on secret remarriage and the extreme case of self-defense.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
The woman is thrice-divorced (bain). The husband denies it. She cannot prove it in court. What are her options? The passage presents two main issues: remarrying secretly and, in extreme cases, killing the husband.
2
Distinguish qada' vs diyaanah
Understand that in Hanafi fiqh, a court ruling (qada') is binding externally, while diyaanah refers to what is permitted between the individual and Allah. A woman may be allowed diyaanatan to marry even if court does not recognize it.
This distinction is critical for many rulings.
3
Trace the ikhtilaf on secret remarriage
Shams al-A'imma al-Ozjandi and others permit it diyaanatan. Other scholars forbid it even diyaanatan. The author seems to incline to permissibility. Note that if the woman is able to flee, she should not remarry secretly.
4
Analyze the dispute on self-defense
When the husband forces intercourse and she cannot escape, can she kill him? Abu Hanifa permits it using poison to avoid retaliation; Judge al-Asbijabi forbids. The later fatwa (al-Multaqat) is against killing.
The woman should not kill herself.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is: she may remarry diyaanatan per al-Ozjandi, and she should not kill the husband but instead flee or ransom herself.
These are the operative rulings in the Hanafi school.

فصل فيما تحل به المطلقة وفي مناقب البزازي : إذا كان العقد بلا ولي بل بعبارة المرأة أو كان بلفظ الهبة أو كان بحضرة فاسقين ثم طلقها ثلاثاً ثم أراد أن تحل له بلا زوج فإنه يرفع الأمر إلى شافعي فيقضي عنها بسبب من الأسباب فلها التحلل ديانة لا قضاء. قال عمر النسفي : سألت عنها السيد أبا شجاع فكتب أنه يجوز . ثم سألته بعد مدة فقال : إنه لا يجوز . والظاهر أنه إنما أجاب في امرأة لا يوثق بها ا.هـ. كذا في شرح المنظومة. وفي البزازية : شهد أن زوجها طلقها ثلاثاً إن كان غائباً ساغ لها أن تتزوج بآخر، وإن كان حاضراً لا لأن الزوج إن أنكرا احتيج إلى القضاء بالفرقة ولا يجوز القضاء بها إلا بحضرة الزوج ا هـ . وفيها : سمعت بطلاق زوجها إياها ثلاثاً ولا تقدر على منعه إلا بقتله إن علمت أنه يقربها تقتله بالدواء ولا تقتل نفسها. وذكر الأوزجندي أنها ترفع الأمر إلى القاضي فإن لم يكن لها بينة تحلفه، فإن حلف فالإثم
