Touch vs Genital Contact and Conditional Oaths
Distinction between oaths about skin contact and genital contact

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between oaths that constitute Ila' and those that do not, and apply the rules of conditional oaths in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Ila' requires an oath of abstaining from intercourse, not mere skin contact.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a common confusion: which oaths create Ila' (an oath of abstinence from intercourse) in Hanafi law? By analyzing the wording 'skin contact' versus 'genital contact' and examining conditional oaths, you will learn the precise conditions that trigger the legal effects of Ila'. Understanding this distinction prevents unintended divorce and ensures oaths are properly classified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the oath
Determine whether the oath explicitly or implicitly refers to vaginal intercourse. Only then does it become Ila' (an oath of abstinence).
Skin contact oaths are not Ila' because touching without intercourse breaks the oath.
2
Analyze the wording for Ila'
If the oath mentions genital contact ('my penis will not touch your vagina'), it is Ila' because it implies intercourse. If it mentions skin contact, it is not.
The key is intent to abstain from intercourse.
3
Examine conditional oaths
A conditional oath like 'if I approach you, you are divorced' is not Ila' because he can fulfill the condition without intercourse (e.g., call her to bed) and then approach later without penalty.
The condition must directly involve intercourse to be Ila'.
4
Apply the time and pregnancy scenario
In the case of a repeated oath during pregnancy, Ila' is established after four months of abstinence, leading to one divorce. The oath is limited to the marriage duration.
After divorce, the old oath does not carry over to future marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيد بالقربان لأنه لو قال والله لا يمس جلدي جلدك لا يكون مولياً لأنه يحنث في يمينه بالمس بدون الجماع في الفرج. ولو قال والله لا يمس فرجي فرجك يكون مولياً لأنه يراد بهذا الكلام الجماع في الفرج. ولو قال لامرأته إن قربتك أو دعوتك إلى فراشي فأنت طالق لا يكون مولياً لأنه يمكنه قربانها من غير وقوع الطلاق بأن يدعوها إلى الفراش فيحنث، ثم يقربها بعد ذلك من غير أن يحنث بالقربان. ولو قال لامرأته إن اغتسلت من جنابتي ما دمت امرأتي فأنت طالق ثلاثاً وأعاد هذا القول وكانت المرأة حاملاً ولم يقربها بعد المقالة حتى وضعت حملها بعد أربعة أشهر فصاعداً فإنها تبين بواحدة عند انقضاء أربعة أشهر لأنه كان مولياً وتنقضي عدتها بوضع الحمل، فإن تزوجها بعد ذلك لا يكون مولياً لو قربها لا يحنث لأن اليمين كانت موقتة إلى بقاء النكاح وبعدما وقعت تطليقة بالإيلاء لا يقع عليها طلاق آخر وإن مضت أربعة أشهر أخرى قبل وضع الحمل لأن المبانة بالإيلاء لا يقع عليها طلاق آخر بحكم ذلك الإيلاء وإن كانت في العدة ما لم تتزوج وتمامه في الخانية.
And he restricted with 'qurbān' because if he says, 'By Allah, my skin will not touch your skin,' he is not an muli because he breaks his oath by touching without intercourse in the vagina. But if he says, 'By Allah, my penis will not touch your vagina,' he is an muli because this speech intends intercourse in the vagina. And if he says to his wife, 'If I approach you or call you to my bed, you are divorced,' he is not an muli because he can approach her without the divorce occurring by calling her to bed, thus breaking the oath, then approaching her afterwards without breaking by the approach. And if he says to his wife, 'If I perform ghusl from janabah while you are my wife, you are triple divorced,' and he repeats this statement, and she is pregnant, and he does not approach her after the statement until she delivers after four months or more, then she becomes separated by one divorce at the end of four months because he was an muli, and her iddah ends with delivery. Then if he marries her after that, he is not an muli; if he approaches her, he does not break the oath because the oath was limited to the duration of the marriage, and after one divorce falls by Ila', no further divorce falls on her by that Ila' even if another four months pass before delivery because the woman separated by Ila' does not receive another divorce by that Ila' even if she is in iddah, until she marries again. The rest is in al-Khaniyya.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage contains two distinct rulings. First, the distinction between oaths about skin-on-skin contact vs. genital contact. Saying 'my skin will not touch your skin' is not Ila' because mere touching without intercourse breaks the oath, and Ila' requires abstention from intercourse. But saying 'my penis will not touch your vagina' is Ila' because it specifically refers to intercourse. Second, the ruling on conditional oaths: saying 'if I approach you, you are divorced' is not Ila' because he can break the condition without committing intercourse (e.g., call her to bed but not have intercourse) and then approach later without penalty. A complex case is examined: a man repeatedly says to his pregnant wife, 'If I perform ghusl from janabah while you are my wife, you are triple divorced,' and he waits until she delivers after four months. This becomes Ila', and one bain divorce occurs at the end of four months, with iddah ending by delivery. If he remarries her afterwards, the old oath does not apply because it was limited to the marriage duration. This illustrates the nuances of timing and conditional oaths.

Key Terms
القربان (al-qurbān): Approach; here means sexual intercourse or intimacy that breaks the oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the oath 'By Allah, my skin will not touch your skin' not considered Ila'?
A) Because skin touch breaks the oath without intercourse
B) Because it is not an oath by Allah
C) Because it does not mention a time limit
D) Because it is too vague

Key Takeaway
The key distinction for Ila' is whether the oath explicitly or implicitly refers to vaginal intercourse; mere skin contact or conditional approach are not Ila'.
